</p>

href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a>)</span></th><td>2018&#160;estimate</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">•&#160;Per capita</div></th><td>$3,354<sup id="cite_ref-imf2_5-1" class="reference"><a scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini</a>&#160;<span style="font-weight:normal;">(2015)</span></th><td>34<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><br /><span style="white-space:nowrap;"><span style="color:orange">medium</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" zone</th><td><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>+5</span> (<a href="/wiki/Tajikistan_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajikistan href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.tj" title=".tj">.tj</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Tajikistan</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ɪ/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">ɪ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Tajikistan.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/03/En-us-Tajikistan.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Tajikistan.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span></span>-, <wbr /><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span></span>-/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a>: <span lang="tg">Тоҷикистон</span> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Persian" title="Help:IPA/Persian">[tɔdʒikisˈtɔn]</a></span>), officially the <b>Republic of Tajikistan</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a>: <span lang="tg">Ҷумҳурии Тоҷикистон</span>, <i>Jumhurii Tojikiston</i>), is a mountainous, <a href="/wiki/Landlocked" class="mw-redirect" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> country in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> with an area of 143,100&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (55,300&#160;sq&#160;mi) and an estimated population of 9,275,828 people.<sup id="cite_ref-worldometers.info_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldometers.info-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> to the north, and <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> to the east. The traditional homelands of the <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">Tajik people</a> include present-day Tajikistan as well as parts of Afghanistan and Uzbekistan.
</p><p>The territory that now constitutes Tajikistan was previously home to several ancient cultures, including the city of <a href="/wiki/Sarazm" title="Sarazm">Sarazm</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>, and was later home to kingdoms ruled by people of different faiths and cultures, including the <a href="/wiki/Bactria-Margiana_Archaeological_Complex" class="mw-redirect" title="Bactria-Margiana Archaeological Complex">Oxus civilisation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andronovo_culture" title="Andronovo culture">Andronovo culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nestorian_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Nestorian Christianity">Nestorian Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">Manichaeism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>. The area has been ruled by numerous empires and dynasties, including the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sasanian_Empire" title="Sasanian Empire">Sasanian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hephthalite_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Hephthalite Empire">Hephthalite Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samanid_Empire" title="Samanid Empire">Samanid Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Timurid_dynasty" title="Timurid dynasty">Timurid dynasty</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara" title="Khanate of Bukhara">Khanate of Bukhara</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, and subsequently the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>. Within the Soviet Union, the <a href="/wiki/National_delimitation_in_the_Soviet_Union#National_delimitation_in_Central_Asia" title="National delimitation in the Soviet Union">country's modern borders were drawn</a> when it was part of <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic">Uzbekistan</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tajik Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">autonomous republic</a> before becoming a <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic">full-fledged Soviet republic</a> in 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 9 September 1991, Tajikistan became an independent sovereign nation when the Soviet Union <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">disintegrated</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Civil_war_in_Tajikistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil war in Tajikistan">civil war</a> was fought almost immediately after independence, lasting from 1992 to 1997. Since the end of the war, newly established political stability and foreign aid have allowed the country's economy to grow. Like all other Central Asian neighbouring states, the country, led by <a href="/wiki/President_of_Tajikistan" title="President of Tajikistan">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon" title="Emomali Rahmon">Emomali Rahmon</a> since 1994, has been criticised by a number of <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">non-governmental organizations</a> for authoritarian leadership, lack of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion_in_Tajikistan" title="Freedom of religion in Tajikistan">religious freedom</a>, corruption and widespread <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Tajikistan" title="Human rights in Tajikistan">violations of human rights</a>.
</p><p>Tajikistan is a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidential republic">presidential republic</a> consisting of four provinces. Most of Tajikistan's population belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik people">Tajik</a> ethnic group,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> who speak <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik Language">Tajik</a> (a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>). <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a> is used as inter-ethnic
language. While the state is constitutionally secular, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Tajikistan" title="Islam in Tajikistan">Islam</a> is practiced by 98% of the population. In the <a href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorno-Badakhshan">Gorno-Badakhshan</a> Oblast of Tajikistan, despite its sparse population, there is large linguistic diversity where <a href="/wiki/Rushani_dialect" title="Rushani dialect">Rushani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shughni_language" title="Shughni language">Shughni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ishkashimi_language" title="Ishkashimi language">Ishkashimi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wakhi_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Wakhi Language">Wakhi</a> and Tajik are some of the languages spoken. Mountains cover more than 90% of the country. It has a <a href="/wiki/Transition_economy" title="Transition economy">transition economy</a> that is highly dependent on <a href="/wiki/Remittances" class="mw-redirect" title="Remittances">remittances</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> production. Tajikistan is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">OIC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">ECO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">SCO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Collective_Security_Treaty_Organization" title="Collective Security Treaty Organization">CSTO</a> as well as an <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> <a href="/wiki/Partnership_for_Peace" title="Partnership for Peace">PfP partner</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span id="Etymology"></span>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik people">Tajik people</a></div>
<p><i>Tajikistan</i> means the "Land of the Tajiks". The <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">suffix</a> "<a href="/wiki/-stan" title="-stan">-stan</a>" is <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a> for "place of"<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> or "country"<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and Tajik is, most likely, the name of a pre-Islamic (before the seventh century A.D.) tribe.<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a>'s 1997 Country Study of Tajikistan, it is difficult to definitively state the origins of the word "Tajik" because the term is "embroiled in twentieth-century political disputes about whether Turkic or Iranian peoples were the original inhabitants of Central Asia."<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tajikistan appeared as <i>Tadjikistan</i> or <i>Tadzhikistan</i> in English prior to 1991. This is due to a transliteration from the <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru">"Таджикистан"</span>. In Russian, there is no single letter j to represent the phoneme /ʤ/, and therefore дж, or dzh, is used. Tadzhikistan is the most common alternate spelling and is widely used in English literature derived from Russian sources.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> "Tadjikistan" is the spelling in French and can occasionally be found in English language texts. The way of writing Tajikistan in the Perso-Arabic script is: <b>تاجیکستان</b>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tajikistan" title="History of Tajikistan">History of Tajikistan</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Samanid_Empire" title="Samanid Empire">Samanid Empire</a></div>
<p>Cultures in the region have been dated back to at least the 4th millennium BCE, including the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Bactria%E2%80%93Margiana_Archaeological_Complex" title="Bactria–Margiana Archaeological Complex">Bactria–Margiana Archaeological Complex</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Andronovo_culture" title="Andronovo culture">Andronovo</a> cultures and the <a href="/wiki/Sarazm" title="Sarazm">pro-urban site of Sarazm</a>, a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The earliest recorded history of the region dates back to about 500 BCE when much, if not all, of modern Tajikistan was part of the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lcweb2.loc.gov_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lcweb2.loc.gov-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Some authors have also suggested that in the 7th and 6th century BCE parts of modern Tajikistan, including territories in the Zeravshan valley, formed part of <a href="/wiki/Kambojas" title="Kambojas">Kambojas</a> before it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
After the region's conquest by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> it became part of the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Bactrian_Kingdom" title="Greco-Bactrian Kingdom">Greco-Bactrian Kingdom</a>, a successor state of Alexander's empire. Northern Tajikistan (the cities of <a href="/wiki/Khujand" title="Khujand">Khujand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panjakent" title="Panjakent">Panjakent</a>) was part of <a href="/wiki/Sogdia" title="Sogdia">Sogdia</a>, a collection of city-states which was overrun by <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">Scythians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yuezhi" title="Yuezhi">Yuezhi</a> nomadic tribes around 150 BCE. The <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> passed through the region and following the expedition of Chinese explorer <a href="/wiki/Zhang_Qian" title="Zhang Qian">Zhang Qian</a> during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Wu_of_Han" title="Emperor Wu of Han">Wudi</a> (141–87 BCE) commercial relations between <a href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Han Dynasty">Han China</a> and Sogdiana flourished.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Sogdians played a major role in facilitating trade and also worked in other capacities, as farmers, carpetweavers, glassmakers, and woodcarvers.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Kushan_Empire" title="Kushan Empire">Kushan Empire</a>, a collection of <a href="/wiki/Yuezhi" title="Yuezhi">Yuezhi</a> tribes, took control of the region in the first century CE and ruled until the 4th century CE during which time <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nestorian_Christianity" class="mw-redirect" title="Nestorian Christianity">Nestorian Christianity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Manichaeism" title="Manichaeism">Manichaeism</a> were all practised in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-Congress_Call_Number_DK851?_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congress_Call_Number_DK851?-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Later the <a href="/wiki/Hephthalite_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Hephthalite Empire">Hephthalite Empire</a>, a collection of nomadic tribes, moved into the region and <a href="/wiki/Arab" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab">Arabs</a> brought <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> in the early eighth century.<sup id="cite_ref-Congress_Call_Number_DK851?_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Congress_Call_Number_DK851?-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Central Asia continued in its role as a commercial crossroads, linking China, the steppes to the north, and the Islamic heartland.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg/220px-MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg/330px-MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg/440px-MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1111" data-file-height="638" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MansurISamanidPaintingHistoryofIran.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Samanid" class="mw-redirect" title="Samanid">Samanid</a> ruler <a href="/wiki/Mansur_I" title="Mansur I">Mansur I</a> (961–976)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria,_Great_Pamir,_May_2nd,_1874.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria%2C_Great_Pamir%2C_May_2nd%2C_1874.png/220px-Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria%2C_Great_Pamir%2C_May_2nd%2C_1874.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria%2C_Great_Pamir%2C_May_2nd%2C_1874.png/330px-Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria%2C_Great_Pamir%2C_May_2nd%2C_1874.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria%2C_Great_Pamir%2C_May_2nd%2C_1874.png/440px-Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria%2C_Great_Pamir%2C_May_2nd%2C_1874.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1107" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomas_Edward_Gordon_Lake_Victoria,_Great_Pamir,_May_2nd,_1874.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>19th-century painting of lake <a href="/wiki/Zorkul" title="Zorkul">Zorkul</a> and a local <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik people">Tajik</a> inhabitant</div></div></div>
<p>It was temporarily under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Tibetan empire">Tibetan empire</a> and Chinese from 650–680 and then under the control of the Umayyads in 710. The <a href="/wiki/Samanids" class="mw-redirect" title="Samanids">Samanid Empire</a>, 819 to 999, restored <a href="/wiki/Persian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian people">Persian</a> control of the region and enlarged the cities of <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a> (both cities are today part of <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>) which became the cultural centres of <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and the region was known as Khorasan. The <a href="/wiki/Kara-Khanid_Khanate" title="Kara-Khanid Khanate">Kara-Khanid Khanate</a> conquered <a href="/wiki/Transoxania" class="mw-redirect" title="Transoxania">Transoxania</a> (which corresponds approximately with modern-day Uzbekistan, Tajikistan, southern Kyrgyzstan and southwest Kazakhstan) and ruled between 999–1211.<sup id="cite_ref-encyclo_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encyclo-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Their arrival in Transoxania signalled a definitive shift from Iranian to Turkic predominance in Central Asia,<sup id="cite_ref-svat_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-svat-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> but gradually the Kara-khanids became assimilated into the Perso-Arab Muslim culture of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/Genghis_Khan" title="Genghis Khan">Genghis Khan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Khwarezmia_and_Eastern_Iran" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongol invasion of Khwarezmia and Eastern Iran">invasion of Khwarezmia</a> in the early 13th century the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> took control over nearly all of Central Asia. In less than a century the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongol Empire</a> broke up and modern Tajikistan came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Chagatai_Khanate" title="Chagatai Khanate">Chagatai Khanate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tamerlane" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamerlane">Tamerlane</a> created the <a href="/wiki/Timurid_dynasty" title="Timurid dynasty">Timurid dynasty</a> and took control of the region in the 14th century.
</p><p>Modern Tajikistan fell under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Bukhara" title="Khanate of Bukhara">Khanate of Bukhara</a> during the 16th century and with the empire's collapse in the 18th century it came under the rule of both the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">Khanate of Kokand</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a> remained intact until the 20th century but during the 19th century, for the second time in world history, a European power (the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>) began to conquer parts of the region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Russian_Tajikistan">Russian Tajikistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Russian Tajikistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Game" title="The Great Game">The Great Game</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_conquest_of_Turkestan" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian conquest of Turkestan">Russian conquest of Turkestan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a></div>
<p>Russian <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">Imperialism</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>'s conquest of <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a> during the late 19th century's <a href="/wiki/Great_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Game">Imperial Era</a>. Between 1864 and 1885, Russia gradually took control of the entire territory of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Turkestan" title="Russian Turkestan">Russian Turkestan</a>, the Tajikistan portion of which had been controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Bukhara" title="Emirate of Bukhara">Emirate of Bukhara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khanate_of_Kokand" title="Khanate of Kokand">Khanate of Kokand</a>. Russia was interested in gaining access to a supply of <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> and in the 1870s attempted to switch cultivation in the region from grain to cotton (a strategy later copied and expanded by the Soviets).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> By 1885 Tajikistan's territory was either ruled by the Russian Empire or its <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal state</a>, the Emirate of Bukhara, nevertheless Tajiks felt little Russian influence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>During the late 19th century the <a href="/wiki/Jadid" title="Jadid">Jadidists</a> established themselves as an Islamic social movement throughout the region. Although the Jadidists were pro-modernization and not necessarily anti-Russian, the Russians viewed the movement as a threat.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Russian troops were required to restore order during uprisings against the Khanate of Kokand between 1910 and 1913. Further violence occurred in July 1916 when demonstrators attacked Russian soldiers in <a href="/wiki/Khujand" title="Khujand">Khujand</a> over the threat of forced <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Despite Russian troops quickly bringing Khujand back under control, clashes continued throughout the year in various locations in Tajikistan.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_Tajikistan">Soviet Tajikistan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Soviet Tajikistan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Basmachi_movement" title="Basmachi movement">Basmachi movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic">Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana,_1921.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana%2C_1921.jpg/220px-Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana%2C_1921.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana%2C_1921.jpg/330px-Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana%2C_1921.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana%2C_1921.jpg/440px-Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana%2C_1921.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1923" data-file-height="1268" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Negotiations_with_basmachs_Fergana,_1921.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soviet negotiations with <i><a href="/wiki/Basmachi_movement" title="Basmachi movement">basmachi</a></i>, 1921</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a> of 1917 guerrillas throughout Central Asia, known as <i><a href="/wiki/Basmachi" class="mw-redirect" title="Basmachi">basmachi</a></i>, waged <a href="/wiki/Kokand_Autonomy" class="mw-redirect" title="Kokand Autonomy">a war</a> against <a href="/wiki/Bolshevik" class="mw-redirect" title="Bolshevik">Bolshevik</a> armies in a futile attempt to maintain independence. The Bolsheviks prevailed after a four-year war, in which <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> and villages were burned down and the population heavily suppressed. Soviet authorities started a campaign of secularisation. Practising <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> was discouraged and repressed, and many mosques, <a href="/wiki/Church_(building)" title="Church (building)">churches</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> were closed.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence of the conflict and Soviet agriculture policies, <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, Tajikistan included, suffered a famine that claimed many lives.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1924, the <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Autonomous_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Tajik Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic">Tajik Autonomous Soviet Socialist Republic</a> was created as a part of <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, but in 1929 the Tajik Soviet Socialist Republic (Tajik SSR) was made a separate constituent republic; however, the predominantly ethnic Tajik cities of <a href="/wiki/Samarkand" title="Samarkand">Samarkand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bukhara" title="Bukhara">Bukhara</a> remained in the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Uzbek Soviet Socialist Republic">Uzbek SSR</a>. Between 1927 and 1934, <a href="/wiki/Collectivisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Collectivisation">collectivisation</a> of agriculture and a rapid expansion of cotton production took place, especially in the southern region.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies.us_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies.us-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Soviet collectivisation policy brought violence against peasants and forced resettlement occurred throughout Tajikistan. Consequently, some peasants fought collectivisation and revived the <a href="/wiki/Basmachi_movement" title="Basmachi movement">Basmachi movement</a>. Some small scale industrial development also occurred during this time along with the expansion of irrigation infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-countrystudies.us_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrystudies.us-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg/220px-Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg/330px-Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg/440px-Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3600" data-file-height="2451" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hammond_Slides_Central_Asia_Unlabeled_15.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Soviet Tajikistan in 1964</div></div></div>
<p>Two rounds of <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Stalin's purges</a> (1927–1934 and 1937–1938) resulted in the expulsion of nearly 10,000 people, from all levels of the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Tajikistan" title="Communist Party of Tajikistan">Communist Party of Tajikistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Purges_1996_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Purges_1996-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Ethnic Russians were sent in to replace those expelled and subsequently Russians dominated party positions at all levels, including the top position of first secretary.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Purges_1996_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Purges_1996-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Between 1926 and 1959 the proportion of <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> among Tajikistan's population grew from less than 1% to 13%.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bobojon_Ghafurov" title="Bobojon Ghafurov">Bobojon Ghafurov</a>, Tajikistan's <a href="/wiki/First_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_Tajikistan" title="First Secretary of the Communist Party of Tajikistan">First Secretary of the Communist Party of Tajikistan</a> from 1946–1956 was the only Tajikistani politician of significance outside of the country during the Soviet Era.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He was followed in office by <a href="/wiki/Tursun_Uljabayev" title="Tursun Uljabayev">Tursun Uljabayev</a> (1956–61), <a href="/wiki/Jabbor_Rasulov" title="Jabbor Rasulov">Jabbor Rasulov</a> (1961–1982), and <a href="/wiki/Rahmon_Nabiyev" title="Rahmon Nabiyev">Rahmon Nabiyev</a> (1982–1985, 1991–1992).
</p><p>Tajiks began to be conscripted into the Soviet Army in 1939 and during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> around 260,000 Tajik citizens fought against Germany, Finland and Japan. Between 60,000 (4%)<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and 120,000 (8%)<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> of Tajikistan's 1,530,000 citizens were killed during World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Following the war and Stalin's reign attempts were made to further expand the agriculture and industry of Tajikistan.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> During 1957–58 <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">Nikita Khrushchev</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Lands_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin Lands Campaign">Virgin Lands Campaign</a> focused attention on Tajikistan, where living conditions, education and industry lagged behind the other <a href="/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Republics of the Soviet Union">Soviet Republics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In the 1980s, Tajikistan had the lowest household saving rate in the USSR,<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> the lowest percentage of households in the two top per capita income groups,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and the lowest rate of university graduates per 1000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> By the late 1980s Tajik nationalists were calling for increased rights. Real disturbances did not occur within the republic until 1990. The following year, the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> collapsed, and Tajikistan declared its independence on 9 September 1991, a day which is now celebrated as the country's <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(Tajikistan)" title="Independence Day (Tajikistan)">Independence Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg/220px-RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg/330px-RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg/440px-RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="689" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAN_archive_466493_Rally_on_Ozodi_square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tajik men and women rally on <a href="/wiki/Dousti_Square" title="Dousti Square">Ozodi square</a> in Dushanbe shortly after independence, 1992.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Tajikistani_Civil_War" title="Tajikistani Civil War">Tajikistani Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg/220px-Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg/330px-Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg/440px-Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg 2x" data-file-width="638" data-file-height="457" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spetsnaz_troopers_during_the_1992_Tajik_war.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Spetsnaz" title="Spetsnaz">Spetsnaz</a> soldiers during the <a href="/wiki/Tajikistani_Civil_War" title="Tajikistani Civil War">civil war</a>, 1992</div></div></div>
<p>The nation almost immediately fell into <a href="/wiki/Tajikistani_Civil_War" title="Tajikistani Civil War">civil war</a> that involved various factions fighting one another; these factions were often distinguished by clan loyalties.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> More than 500,000 residents fled during this time because of persecution, increased poverty and better economic opportunities in the West or in other former Soviet republics.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon" title="Emomali Rahmon">Emomali Rahmon</a> came to power in 1992, defeating former prime minister <a href="/wiki/Abdumalik_Abdullajanov" title="Abdumalik Abdullajanov">Abdumalik Abdullajanov</a> in a November presidential election with 58% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The elections took place shortly after the end of the war, and Tajikistan was in a state of complete devastation. The estimated dead numbered over 100,000. Around 1.2 million people were <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a> inside and outside of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-United_Nations_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Nations-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, a <a href="/wiki/Ceasefire" title="Ceasefire">ceasefire</a> was reached between Rahmon and opposition parties under the guidance of Gerd D. Merrem, Special Representative to the Secretary General, a result widely praised as a successful United Nations peacekeeping initiative. The ceasefire guaranteed 30% of ministerial positions would go to the <a href="/wiki/United_Tajik_Opposition" title="United Tajik Opposition">opposition</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tajikistani_presidential_election,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajikistani presidential election, 1999">Elections</a> were held in 1999, though they were criticised by opposition parties and foreign observers as unfair and Rahmon was re-elected with 98% of the vote. <a href="/wiki/Tajik_presidential_election,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik presidential election, 2006">Elections in 2006</a> were again won by Rahmon (with 79% of the vote) and he began his third term in office. Several opposition parties boycotted the 2006 election and the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> (OSCE) criticised it, although observers from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> claimed the elections were legal and transparent.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Rahmon's administration came under further criticism from the OSCE in October 2010 for its censorship and repression of the media. The OSCE claimed that the Tajik Government censored Tajik and foreign websites and instituted tax inspections on independent printing houses that led to the cessation of printing activities for a number of independent newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> border troops were stationed along the Tajik–Afghan border until summer 2005. Since the <a href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="September 11, 2001 attacks">September 11, 2001 attacks</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> troops have been stationed at the <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Dushanbe Airport">Dushanbe Airport</a> in support of air operations of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/International_Security_Assistance_Force" title="International Security Assistance Force">International Security Assistance Force</a> in <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">Marine Corps</a> personnel periodically visit Tajikistan to conduct joint training missions of up to several weeks duration. The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a> rebuilt the <a href="/wiki/Ayni_Air_Base" title="Ayni Air Base">Ayni Air Base</a>, a military airport located 15&#160;km southwest of Dushanbe, at a cost of $70 million, completing the repairs in September 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> It is now the main base of the Tajikistan air force. There have been talks with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> concerning use of the Ayni facility,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> and Russia continues to maintain a large base on the outskirts of Dushanbe.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg/220px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg/330px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg/440px-%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2880" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%D0%9D%D0%B0%D0%B2%D1%80%D3%AF%D0%B7_%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%94%D0%9C%D0%A2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tajiks in traditional dress in 2017</div></div></div>
<p>In 2010, there were concerns among Tajik officials that Islamic militarism in the east of the country was on the rise following the escape of 25 militants from a Tajik prison in August, an ambush that killed 28 Tajik soldiers in the <a href="/wiki/Rasht_Valley" title="Rasht Valley">Rasht Valley</a> in September,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and another ambush in the valley in October that killed 30 soldiers,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> followed by fighting outside <a href="/wiki/Gharm" title="Gharm">Gharm</a> that left 3 militants dead. To date the country's Interior Ministry asserts that the central government maintains full control over the country's east, and the military operation in the Rasht Valley was concluded in November 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/2012_Gorno-Badakhshan_clashes" title="2012 Gorno-Badakhshan clashes">fighting erupted again</a> in July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
In 2015, Russia sent more troops to Tajikistan.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2015, Tajikistan's national security suffered a serious setback when Colonel <a href="/wiki/Gulmurod_Khalimov" title="Gulmurod Khalimov">Gulmurod Khalimov</a>, commander of the special-purpose police unit (OMON) of the Interior Ministry, defected to the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Tajikistan" title="Politics of Tajikistan">Politics of Tajikistan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Tajikistan" title="Elections in Tajikistan">Elections in Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Tajikistan" title="Foreign relations of Tajikistan">Foreign relations of Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Tajikistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Tajikistan">Military of Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Tajikistan" title="Human rights in Tajikistan">Human rights in Tajikistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tajikistani_Civil_War" title="Tajikistani Civil War">Tajikistani Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg/220px-Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg/330px-Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg/440px-Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2410" data-file-height="1494" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dushanbe_Presidential_Palace_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Palace of Nations in <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe" title="Dushanbe">Dushanbe</a></div></div></div>
<p>Almost immediately after independence, Tajikistan was plunged into a civil war that saw various factions fighting one another. These factions were supported by foreign countries including <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>. Russia and Iran focused on keeping peace in the warring nation to decrease the chance of <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> involvement. Most notably, Russia backed the pro-government faction and deployed troops from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">Commonwealth of Independent States</a> to guard the Tajikistan-Afghan border.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> All but 25,000 of the more than 400,000 ethnic Russians, who were mostly employed in industry, fled to Russia. By 1997, the war had cooled down, and a central government began to take form, with peaceful elections in 1999.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg/170px-Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg/255px-Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg/340px-Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="554" data-file-height="739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Emomali_Rahmonov_2001Nov03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/President_of_Tajikistan" title="President of Tajikistan">President of Tajikistan</a> <a href="/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon" title="Emomali Rahmon">Emomali Rahmon</a> has ruled the country since 1994.</div></div></div>
<p>"Longtime observers of Tajikistan often characterize the country as profoundly averse to risk and skeptical of promises of reform, a political passivity they trace to the country’s ruinous civil war," Ilan Greenberg wrote in a news article in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> just before the country's November 2006 presidential election.<sup id="cite_ref-greenberg_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenberg-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tajikistan is officially a republic, and holds <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Tajikistan" title="Elections in Tajikistan">elections</a> for the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Tajikistan" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Presidents of Tajikistan">presidency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>, operating under a <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential system</a>. It is, however, a <a href="/wiki/Dominant-party_system" title="Dominant-party system">dominant-party system</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Democratic_Party_of_Tajikistan" title="People&#39;s Democratic Party of Tajikistan">People's Democratic Party of Tajikistan</a> routinely has a vast majority in <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">Parliament</a>. <a href="/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon" title="Emomali Rahmon">Emomali Rahmon</a> has held the office of <a href="/wiki/President_of_Tajikistan" title="President of Tajikistan">President of Tajikistan</a> continuously since November 1994. The Prime Minister is <a href="/wiki/Kokhir_Rasulzoda" title="Kokhir Rasulzoda">Kokhir Rasulzoda</a>, the First Deputy Prime Minister is Matlubkhon Davlatov and the two Deputy Prime Ministers are Murodali Alimardon and Ruqiya Qurbanova.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_(2017-02-27)_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_%282017-02-27%29_2.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_%282017-02-27%29_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_%282017-02-27%29_2.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_%282017-02-27%29_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_%282017-02-27%29_2.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_%282017-02-27%29_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1880" data-file-height="1160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_and_Emomali_Rahmon_(2017-02-27)_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>President of Tajikistan <a href="/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon" title="Emomali Rahmon">Emomali Rahmon</a> with Russian president <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The parliamentary elections of 2005 aroused many accusations from opposition parties and international observers that President <a href="/wiki/Emomali_Rahmon" title="Emomali Rahmon">Emomali Rahmon</a> corruptly manipulates the election process and unemployment. The most recent elections, in February 2010, saw the ruling PDPT lose four seats in Parliament, yet still maintain a comfortable majority. The <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> election observers said the 2010 polling "failed to meet many key OSCE commitments" and that "these elections failed on many basic democratic standards."<sup id="cite_ref-economistchange_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economistchange-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC2010election_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2010election-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The government insisted that only minor violations had occurred, which would not affect the will of the Tajik people.<sup id="cite_ref-economistchange_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economistchange-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BBC2010election_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC2010election-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The presidential election held on 6 November 2006 was boycotted by "mainline" opposition parties, including the 23,000-member <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Renaissance_Party_of_Tajikistan" title="Islamic Renaissance Party of Tajikistan">Islamic Renaissance Party</a>. Four remaining opponents "all but endorsed the incumbent", Rahmon.<sup id="cite_ref-greenberg_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenberg-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Tajikistan gave Iran its support in Iran's membership bid to join the <a href="/wiki/Shanghai_Cooperation_Organisation" title="Shanghai Cooperation Organisation">Shanghai Cooperation Organisation</a>, after a meeting between the Tajik President and the Iranian foreign minister.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Freedom of the press is ostensibly officially guaranteed by the government, but independent press outlets remain restricted, as does a substantial amount of web content. According to the Institute for War &amp; Peace Reporting, access is blocked to local and foreign websites including avesta.tj, Tjknews.com, ferghana.ru, centrasia.org and journalists are often obstructed from reporting on controversial events. In practice, no public criticism of the regime is tolerated and all direct protest is severely suppressed and does not receive coverage in the local media.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2019, UN ambassadors of 37 countries, including Tajikistan, have signed a joint letter to the <a href="/wiki/UNHRC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNHRC">UNHRC</a> defending China's <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_re-education_camps" title="Xinjiang re-education camps">treatment of Uyghurs</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang" title="Xinjiang">Xinjiang</a> region.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Tajikistan" title="Geography of Tajikistan">Geography of Tajikistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg/220px-Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg/330px-Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg/440px-Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_satellite_photo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Satellite photograph of Tajikistan</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/220px-Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/330px-Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/440px-Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1900" data-file-height="1463" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tajikistan map of Köppen climate classification</div></div></div>
<p>Tajikistan is <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked</a>, and is the smallest nation in Central Asia by area. It lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/36th_parallel_north" title="36th parallel north">36°</a> and <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/67th_meridian_east" title="67th meridian east">67°</a> and <a href="/wiki/75th_meridian_east" title="75th meridian east">75° E</a>. It is covered by mountains of the <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir</a> range, and more than fifty percent of the country is over 3,000 metres (9,800&#160;ft) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. The only major areas of lower land are in the north (part of the <a href="/wiki/Fergana_Valley" title="Fergana Valley">Fergana Valley</a>), and in the southern <a href="/wiki/Kofarnihon_River" title="Kofarnihon River">Kofarnihon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vakhsh_River" title="Vakhsh River">Vakhsh</a> river valleys, which form the Amu Darya. <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe" title="Dushanbe">Dushanbe</a> is located on the southern slopes above the Kofarnihon valley.
</p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/Amu_Darya" title="Amu Darya">Amu Darya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Panj_River" title="Panj River">Panj</a> rivers mark the border with Afghanistan, and the glaciers in Tajikistan's mountains are the major source of <a href="/wiki/Runoff_(water)" class="mw-redirect" title="Runoff (water)">runoff</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Aral_Sea" title="Aral Sea">Aral Sea</a>. There are over 900 rivers in Tajikistan longer than 10 kilometres.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Tajikistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Provinces of Tajikistan">Provinces of Tajikistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Tajikistan" title="Districts of Tajikistan">Districts of Tajikistan</a></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046874">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .mobile-float-reset{float:none!important;width:100%!important}}.mw-parser-output .stack-container{box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-left{float:left;clear:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-right{float:right;clear:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-object{margin:1px;overflow:hidden}</style><div class="mw-stack stack-container stack-right mobile-float-reset"><div style="overflow: hidden; margin: 1px;"><div class="noresize" style="height: 220px; width: 300px; "><map name="ImageMap_96d1d70d7930ffae"><area href="/wiki/Sughd_Province" shape="rect" coords="52,55,78,91" alt="Sughd Province" title="Sughd Province" /><area href="/wiki/Districts_of_Republican_Subordination" shape="rect" coords="100,85,129,111" alt="Districts of Republican Subordination" title="Districts of Republican Subordination" /><area href="/wiki/Khatlon_Province" shape="rect" coords="53,141,81,169" alt="Khatlon Province" title="Khatlon Province" /><area href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Province" shape="rect" coords="200,124,235,161" alt="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province" title="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province" /></map><img alt="A clickable map of Tajikistan exhibiting its four provinces." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Tajikistan_provinces.png/300px-Tajikistan_provinces.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="220" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/Tajikistan_provinces.png 1.5x" data-file-width="335" data-file-height="246" usemap="#ImageMap_96d1d70d7930ffae" /><div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_provinces.png" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;" /></a></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg/220px-Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg/330px-Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg/440px-Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajik_mountains_edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mountains of Tajikistan</div></div></div>
<p>Tajikistan consists of 4 administrative divisions. These are the provinces (<a href="/wiki/Viloyat" class="mw-redirect" title="Viloyat">viloyat</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Sughd" class="mw-redirect" title="Sughd">Sughd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khatlon" class="mw-redirect" title="Khatlon">Khatlon</a>, the autonomous province of <a href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province">Gorno-Badakhshan</a> (abbreviated as GBAO), and the <a href="/wiki/Region_of_Republican_Subordination" class="mw-redirect" title="Region of Republican Subordination">Region of Republican Subordination</a> (RRP&#160;– Raiony Respublikanskogo Podchineniya in <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Russian" title="Romanization of Russian">transliteration</a> from Russian or NTJ – Ноҳияҳои тобеи ҷумҳурӣ in <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a>; formerly known as <a href="/wiki/Karotegin_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Karotegin Province">Karotegin Province</a>). Each region is divided into several districts, (<a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a>: <span lang="tg">Ноҳия</span>, <i>nohiya</i> or <i>raion</i>), which in turn are subdivided into <i>jamoats</i> (village-level self-governing units) and then villages (<i>qyshloqs</i>). As of 2006<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were 58 districts and 367 jamoats in Tajikistan.<sup id="cite_ref-pop2008_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop2008-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
