href="/wiki/File:%D0%92%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%88%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%D0%A3%D1%80%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%B1%D1%83%D0%B7._%D0%92%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D0%B8_-_%D0%9F%D0%B8%D0%BA_%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0._%D0%92%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B7%D1%83_-_%D0%BE%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BE_%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BB%D1%8C.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Karakul_(Tajikistan)" title="Karakul (Tajikistan)">Karakul lake</a></div></div></div>
<p>About 2% of the country's area is covered by lakes, the best known of which are the following:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kayrakkum_Reservoir" title="Kayrakkum Reservoir">Kayrakum (Qairoqqum) Reservoir</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sughd" class="mw-redirect" title="Sughd">Sughd</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iskanderkul" title="Iskanderkul">Iskanderkul</a> (<a href="/wiki/Fann_Mountains" title="Fann Mountains">Fann Mountains</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kulikalon_Lakes" title="Kulikalon Lakes">Kulikalon</a> (Kul-i Kalon) (<a href="/wiki/Fann_Mountains" title="Fann Mountains">Fann Mountains</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nurek_Dam" title="Nurek Dam">Nurek Reservoir</a> (<a href="/wiki/Khatlon" class="mw-redirect" title="Khatlon">Khatlon</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karakul_(Tajikistan)" title="Karakul (Tajikistan)">Karakul</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_language" title="Kyrgyz language">Kyrgyz</a>: <i>Кара-Көл</i>; eastern <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sarez_Lake" title="Sarez Lake">Sarez</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Shadau_Lake" class="mw-redirect" title="Shadau Lake">Shadau Lake</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zorkul" title="Zorkul">Zorkul</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir</a>)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Tajikistan" title="Economy of Tajikistan">Economy of Tajikistan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Tajikistan" title="Agriculture in Tajikistan">Agriculture in Tajikistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg/220px-Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg/330px-Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg/440px-Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1080" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Young_Tajikistani_dry_fruit_seller.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Tajik dry fruit seller</div></div></div>
<p>Nearly 47% of Tajikistan's GDP comes from <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> <a href="/wiki/Remittances" class="mw-redirect" title="Remittances">remittances</a> (mostly from Tajiks working in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The current economic situation remains fragile, largely owing to <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, uneven economic reforms, and economic mismanagement. With foreign revenue precariously dependent upon remittances from migrant workers overseas and exports of aluminium and cotton, the economy is highly vulnerable to external shocks. In FY 2000, international assistance remained an essential source of support for rehabilitation programs that reintegrated former civil war combatants into the civilian economy, which helped keep the peace. International assistance also was necessary to address the second year of severe <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">drought</a> that resulted in a continued shortfall of food production. On 21 August 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="Red Cross">Red Cross</a> announced that a <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famine</a> was striking Tajikistan, and called for international aid for Tajikistan and <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>; however, access to food remains a problem today. In January 2012, 680,152 of the people living in Tajikistan were living with <a href="/wiki/Food_insecurity" class="mw-redirect" title="Food insecurity">food insecurity</a>. Out of those, 676,852 were at risk of Phase 3 (Acute Food and Livelihoods Crisis) food insecurity and 3,300 were at risk of Phase 4 (Humanitarian Emergency). Those with the highest risk of food insecurity were living in the remote <a href="/wiki/Murghob_District" title="Murghob District">Murghob District</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province">GBAO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Talco.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Talco.jpg/220px-Talco.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Talco.jpg/330px-Talco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Talco.jpg/440px-Talco.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="853" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Talco.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/TadAZ" class="mw-redirect" title="TadAZ">TadAZ</a> aluminium smelting plant, in Tursunzoda, is the largest aluminium manufacturing plant in <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">Central Asia</a>, and Tajikistan's chief industrial asset.</div></div></div>
<p>Tajikistan's economy grew substantially after the war. The GDP of Tajikistan expanded at an average rate of 9.6% over the period of 2000–2007 according to the World Bank data. This improved Tajikistan's position among other Central Asian countries (namely <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenia</a> and Uzbekistan), which seem to have degraded economically ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The primary sources of income in Tajikistan are <a href="/wiki/Aluminium" title="Aluminium">aluminium</a> production, cotton growing and remittances from migrant workers.<sup id="cite_ref-usstate2_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usstate2-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Cotton accounts for 60% of agricultural output, supporting 75% of the rural population, and using 45% of irrigated arable land.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The aluminium industry is represented by the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Tajik_Aluminum_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik Aluminum Company">Tajik Aluminum Company</a> – the biggest aluminium plant in Central Asia and one of the biggest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-expert.ru2_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expert.ru2-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tajikistan's rivers, such as the <a href="/wiki/Vakhsh_River" title="Vakhsh River">Vakhsh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Panj_River" title="Panj River">Panj</a>, have great hydropower potential, and the government has focused on attracting investment for projects for internal use and electricity exports. Tajikistan is home to the <a href="/wiki/Nurek_Dam" title="Nurek Dam">Nurek Dam</a>, the second highest dam in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-dams2_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dams2-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>  Lately, Russia's <a href="/wiki/RAO_UES" title="RAO UES">RAO UES</a> energy giant has been working on the Sangtuda-1 hydroelectric power station (670&#160;MW capacity) commenced operations on 18 January 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-vesti2_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vesti2-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-todayenergy2_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-todayenergy2-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Other projects at the development stage include Sangtuda-2 by Iran, Zerafshan by the Chinese company <a href="/wiki/SinoHydro" class="mw-redirect" title="SinoHydro">SinoHydro</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Rogun_Dam" title="Rogun Dam">Rogun power plant</a> that, at a projected height of 335 metres (1,099&#160;ft), would supersede the Nurek Dam as highest in the world if it is brought to completion.<sup id="cite_ref-irna2_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irna2-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rferl12_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rferl12-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> A planned project, <a href="/wiki/CASA-1000" title="CASA-1000">CASA-1000</a>, will transmit 1000 MW of surplus electricity from Tajikistan to Pakistan with power transit through Afghanistan. The total length of transmission line is 750&#160;km while the project is planned to be on Public-Private Partnership basis with the support of WB, IFC, ADB and IDB. The project cost is estimated to be around US$865 million.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Other energy resources include sizeable coal deposits and smaller reserves of natural gas and petroleum.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="959" data-file-height="748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of Tajikistan's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories</div></div></div>
<p>In 2014 Tajikistan was the world's most <a href="/wiki/Remittance" title="Remittance">remittance</a>-dependent economy with remittances accounting for 49% of GDP and expected to fall by 40% in 2015 due to the economic crisis in the Russian Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-eurasianet.org_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurasianet.org-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Tajik migrant workers abroad, mainly in the Russian Federation, have become by far the main source of income for millions of Tajikistan's people<sup id="cite_ref-wb-note32_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-note32-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and with the 2014–2015 downturn in the Russian economy the World Bank has predicted large numbers of young Tajik men will return home and face few economic prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-eurasianet.org_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eurasianet.org-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to some estimates about 20% of the population lives on less than US$1.25 per day.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Migration from Tajikistan and the consequent remittances have been unprecedented in their magnitude and economic impact. In 2010, remittances from Tajik labour migrants totalled an estimated $2.1 billion US dollars, an increase from 2009. Tajikistan has achieved transition from a planned to a market economy without substantial and protracted recourse to aid (of which it by now receives only negligible amounts), and by purely market-based means, simply by exporting its main commodity of comparative advantage&#160;— cheap labour.<sup id="cite_ref-imf3_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imf3-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> The World Bank Tajikistan Policy Note 2006 concludes that remittances have played an important role as one of the drivers of Tajikistan's economic growth during the past several years, have increased incomes, and as a result helped significantly reduce poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-wb-policynote2_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wb-policynote2-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Drug trafficking is the major illegal source of income in Tajikistan<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> as it is an important transit country for Afghan <a href="/wiki/Narcotics" class="mw-redirect" title="Narcotics">narcotics</a> bound for Russian and, to a lesser extent, Western European markets; some <a href="/wiki/Opium_poppy" class="mw-redirect" title="Opium poppy">opium poppy</a> is also raised locally for the domestic market.<sup id="cite_ref-Silk2_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silk2-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>  However, with the increasing assistance from international organisations, such as UNODC, and co-operation with the US, Russian, EU and Afghan authorities a level of progress on the fight against illegal drug-trafficking is being achieved.<sup id="cite_ref-edm12_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edm12-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Tajikistan holds third place in the world for <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a> and raw <a href="/wiki/Opium" title="Opium">opium</a> confiscations (1216.3&#160;kg of heroin and 267.8&#160;kg of raw opium in the first half of 2006).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Drug money corrupts the country's government; according to some experts the well-known personalities that fought on both sides of the <a href="/wiki/Civil_war_in_Tajikistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Civil war in Tajikistan">civil war</a> and have held the positions in the government after the armistice was signed are now involved in the drug trade.<sup id="cite_ref-Silk2_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Silk2-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/UNODC" class="mw-redirect" title="UNODC">UNODC</a> is working with Tajikistan to strengthen border crossings, provide training, and set up joint interdiction teams. It also helped to establish Tajikistani Drug Control Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-fight2_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fight2-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Tajikistan is also an active member of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Cooperation_Organization" title="Economic Cooperation Organization">Economic Cooperation Organization</a> (ECO).
</p><p>Besides Russia, China is one of the major economic and trade partners of Dushanbe. Tajikistan belongs to the group of countries with a high debt trap risk associated with Chinese investment within the Belt and Road Initiative (BRI) meaning that excessive reliance on Chinese loans may weaken country's ability to manage its external debt in a sustainable way.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Tajikistan" title="Transport in Tajikistan">Transport in Tajikistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg/220px-Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg/330px-Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg/440px-Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Duschanbe_Bahnhof.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dushanbe" title="Dushanbe">Dushanbe</a> railway station</div></div></div>
<p>In 2013 Tajikistan, like many of the other Central Asian countries, was experiencing major development in its transportation sector.
</p><p>As a landlocked country Tajikistan has no ports and the majority of transportation is via roads, air, and rail. In recent years Tajikistan has pursued agreements with <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> to gain port access in those countries via <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>. In 2009, an agreement was made between Tajikistan, Pakistan, and Afghanistan to improve and build a 1,300&#160;km (810&#160;mi) highway and rail system connecting the three countries to Pakistan's ports. The proposed route would go through the <a href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province">Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province</a> in the eastern part of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-pak_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pak-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> And in 2012, the presidents of Tajikistan, Afghanistan, and Iran signed an agreement to construct roads and railways as well as oil, gas, and water pipelines to connect the three countries.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Tajikistan" title="Rail transport in Tajikistan">Rail transport in Tajikistan</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Railroad">railroad</a> system totals only 680 kilometres (420&#160;mi) of track,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> all of it <span class="nowrap">1,520&#160;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">4&#160;ft&#160;<span class="frac">11<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>27</sup>&#8260;<sub>32</sub></span>&#160;in</span>) <a href="/wiki/Russian_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian gauge">broad gauge</a>. The principal segments are in the southern region and connect the capital with the industrial areas of the <a href="/wiki/Hisor" title="Hisor">Hisor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vakhsh,_Tajikistan" title="Vakhsh, Tajikistan">Vakhsh</a> valleys and with <a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Most international freight traffic is carried by train.<sup id="cite_ref-tajikistanmission.ch_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tajikistanmission.ch-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The recently constructed <a href="/wiki/Qurghonteppa" title="Qurghonteppa">Qurghonteppa</a>–<a href="/wiki/Kulob" title="Kulob">Kulob</a> railway connected the <a href="/wiki/Kulob_District" title="Kulob District">Kulob District</a> with the central area of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-tajikistanmission.ch_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tajikistanmission.ch-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dushanbe_Airport_(DYU).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Dushanbe_Airport_%28DYU%29.jpg/220px-Dushanbe_Airport_%28DYU%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Dushanbe_Airport_%28DYU%29.jpg/330px-Dushanbe_Airport_%28DYU%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Dushanbe_Airport_%28DYU%29.jpg/440px-Dushanbe_Airport_%28DYU%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dushanbe_Airport_(DYU).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The old terminal building at <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe_International_Airport" title="Dushanbe International Airport">Dushanbe International Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 2009 Tajikistan had 26 airports, 18 of which had paved runways, of which two had runways longer than 3,000 meters.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_83-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The country's main airport is <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe_International_Airport" title="Dushanbe International Airport">Dushanbe International Airport</a> which as of April 2015, had regularly scheduled flights to major cities in Russia, Central Asia, as well as Delhi, Dubai, Frankfurt, Istanbul, Kabul, Tehran, and Ürümqi amongst others. There are also international flights, mainly to Russia, from <a href="/wiki/Khujand_Airport" title="Khujand Airport">Khujand Airport</a> in the northern part of the country as well as limited international services from <a href="/wiki/Kulob_Airport" title="Kulob Airport">Kulob Airport</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Qurghonteppa_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Qurghonteppa International Airport">Qurghonteppa International Airport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Khorog_Airport" title="Khorog Airport">Khorog Airport</a> is a domestic airport and also the only airport in the sparsely populated eastern half of the country.
</p><p>Tajikistan has one major airline (<a href="/wiki/Somon_Air" title="Somon Air">Somon Air</a>) and is also serviced by over a dozen foreign airlines.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The total length of roads in the country is 27,800 kilometres. Automobiles account for more than 90% of the total volume of passenger transportation and more than 80% of domestic freight transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-tajikistanmission.ch_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tajikistanmission.ch-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004 the <a href="/wiki/Tajik%E2%80%93Afghan_Friendship_Bridge" title="Tajik–Afghan Friendship Bridge">Tajik–Afghan Friendship Bridge</a> between Afghanistan and Tajikistan was built, improving the country's access to <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a>. The bridge was built by the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-usace_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usace-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> many highway and tunnel construction projects are underway or have recently been completed. Major projects include rehabilitation of the Dushanbe – Chanak (Uzbek border), Dushanbe – Kulma (Chinese border), and Kurgan-Tube – Nizhny Pyanj (Afghan border) highways, and construction of tunnels under the mountain passes of <a href="/wiki/Anzob_Tunnel" title="Anzob Tunnel">Anzob</a>, Shakhristan, Shar-Shar<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> and Chormazak.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> These were supported by international donor countries.<sup id="cite_ref-tajikistanmission.ch_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tajikistanmission.ch-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Tajikistan" title="Demographics of Tajikistan">Demographics of Tajikistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Tajikistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/280px-Tajikistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="131" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Tajikistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/420px-Tajikistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/97/Tajikistan%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 2x" data-file-width="437" data-file-height="204" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajikistan,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tajikistan: trends in its Human Development Index indicator 1970–2010</div></div></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg/220px-Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg/330px-Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg/440px-Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Women_of_Dushanbe_.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Group of Tajik women</div></div></div>
<p>Tajikistan has a population of 9,275,832 people,<sup id="cite_ref-worldometers.info_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldometers.info-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> of which 70% are under the age of 30 and 35% are between the ages of 14 and 30.<sup id="cite_ref-youtube.com_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-youtube.com-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik people">Tajiks</a> who speak <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a> (a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>) are the main ethnic group, although there are sizeable minorities of <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a>, whose numbers are declining due to emigration.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pamiri_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pamiri people">Pamiris</a> of <a href="/wiki/Badakhshan" title="Badakhshan">Badakhshan</a>, a small population of <a href="/wiki/Yaghnobi_people" title="Yaghnobi people">Yaghnobi people</a>, and a sizeable minority of <a href="/wiki/Ismailis" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismailis">Ismailis</a> are all considered to belong to the larger group of Tajiks. All citizens of Tajikistan are called <a href="/wiki/Tajikistanis" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajikistanis">Tajikistanis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_83-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1989, ethnic <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Tajikistan" title="Russians in Tajikistan">Russians in Tajikistan</a> made up 7.6% of the population, but they are now less than 0.5%, after the civil war spurred Russian emigration.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/History_of_Germans_in_Russia_and_the_Soviet_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Germans in Russia and the Soviet Union">ethnic German</a> population of Tajikistan has also declined due to emigration: having topped at 38,853 in 1979, it has almost vanished since the collapse of the Soviet Union.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The official and vernacular language of Tajikistan is <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik</a>, a variety of <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, although Russian is routinely used in business and communication. The Constitution mentions Russian as the "language for inter-ethnic communication." An amendment passed in 2009 was thought to remove all official roles for Russian,<sup id="cite_ref-RFE/RL_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RFE/RL-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> although the status was later re-instated, leaving Russian as permissible for law-making but still urging that official communications take place in Tajik.<sup id="cite_ref-RIA-RU_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIA-RU-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lenta.ru/news/2011/06/09_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lenta.ru/news/2011/06/09-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> Russian is regularly used between different ethnic groups in the country and thereby fulfilling its stated constitutional role.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">Employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2009 nearly one million <a href="/wiki/Tajiks" title="Tajiks">Tajiks</a> worked abroad (mainly in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> More than 70% of the female population lives in traditional villages.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Tajikistan" title="Culture of Tajikistan">Culture of Tajikistan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Tajikistan" title="Music of Tajikistan">Music of Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajik_literature" title="Tajik literature">Tajik literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Public_holidays_in_Tajikistan" title="Public holidays in Tajikistan">Public holidays in Tajikistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tajik_cuisine" title="Tajik cuisine">Tajik cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Yaghnobi_boy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Yaghnobi_boy.jpg/170px-Yaghnobi_boy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Yaghnobi_boy.jpg/255px-Yaghnobi_boy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Yaghnobi_boy.jpg/340px-Yaghnobi_boy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="518" data-file-height="535" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Yaghnobi_boy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yaghnobi_people" title="Yaghnobi people">Yaghnobi</a> boy</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tajik_language" title="Tajik language">Tajik language</a> is the mother tongue of around 80% of the citizens of Tajikistan. The main urban centres in today's Tajikistan include <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe" title="Dushanbe">Dushanbe</a> (the capital), <a href="/wiki/Khujand" title="Khujand">Khujand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kulob" title="Kulob">Kulob</a>, <a href="/wiki/Panjakent" title="Panjakent">Panjakent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qurghonteppa" title="Qurghonteppa">Qurghonteppa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khorugh" title="Khorugh">Khorugh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Istaravshan" title="Istaravshan">Istaravshan</a>. There are also <a href="/wiki/Uzbeks" title="Uzbeks">Uzbek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_people" title="Kyrgyz people">Kyrgyz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russian</a> minorities.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pamiri_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Pamiri people">Pamiri people</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province">Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Province</a> in the southeast, bordering Afghanistan and China, though considered part of the <a href="/wiki/Tajik_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik people">Tajik ethnicity</a>, nevertheless are distinct linguistically and culturally from most Tajiks. In contrast to the mostly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni Muslim">Sunni Muslim</a> residents of the rest of Tajikistan, the Pamiris overwhelmingly follow the <a href="/wiki/Ismaili" class="mw-redirect" title="Ismaili">Ismaili</a> branch of Shia Islam, and speak a number of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Iranian" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Iranian">Eastern Iranian</a> languages, including <a href="/wiki/Shughni_language" title="Shughni language">Shughni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rushani_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Rushani language">Rushani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khufi_language" title="Khufi language">Khufi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wakhi_language" title="Wakhi language">Wakhi</a>. Isolated in the highest parts of the <a href="/wiki/Pamir_Mountains" title="Pamir Mountains">Pamir</a> Mountains, they have preserved many ancient cultural traditions and folk arts that have been largely lost elsewhere in the country.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Yaghnobi_people" title="Yaghnobi people">Yaghnobi people</a> live in mountainous areas of northern Tajikistan. The estimated number of Yaghnobis is now about 25,000. Forced migrations in the 20th century decimated their numbers. They speak the <a href="/wiki/Yaghnobi_language" title="Yaghnobi language">Yaghnobi language</a>, which is the only direct modern descendant of the ancient <a href="/wiki/Sogdian_language" title="Sogdian language">Sogdian language</a>.
</p><p>Tajikistan artisans created the <a href="/wiki/Dushanbe_Tea_House" title="Dushanbe Tea House">Dushanbe Tea House</a>, which was presented in 1988 as a gift to the sister city of <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder, Colorado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Tajikistan" title="Religion in Tajikistan">Religion in Tajikistan</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Tajikistan" title="Islam in Tajikistan">Islam in Tajikistan</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tbody><tr style="background:#ddd"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Tajikistan, 2010<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>
<tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;">

<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:blue; width:1.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>

</tr>

</tr>

</tbody></table>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg/170px-Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg/255px-Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg/340px-Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="427" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Abdullokhon_Mosque_Isfara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> in <a href="/wiki/Isfara" title="Isfara">Isfara</a>, Tajikistan</div></div></div>
<p>Sunni Islam of the <a href="/wiki/Hanafi" title="Hanafi">Hanafi</a> school has been officially recognised by the government since 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Tajikistan considers itself a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a> with a Constitution providing for freedom of religion. The Government has declared two Islamic holidays, <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eid_al-Adha" title="Eid al-Adha">Eid al-Adha</a>, as state holidays. According to a <a href="/wiki/US_State_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> release and Pew research group, the population of Tajikistan is 98% <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>. Approximately 87%–95% of them are <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a> and roughly 3% are <a href="/wiki/Shia" class="mw-redirect" title="Shia">Shia</a> and roughly 7% are <a href="/wiki/Non-denominational_Muslims" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-denominational Muslims">non-denominational Muslims</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The remaining 2% of the population are followers of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodoxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoroastrianism" title="Zoroastrianism">Zoroastrianism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>. A great majority of Muslims fast during Ramadan, although only about one third in the countryside and 10% in the cities observe daily prayer and dietary restrictions.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Bukharan_Jews" title="Bukharan Jews">Bukharan Jews</a> had lived in Tajikistan since the 2nd century BCE, but today almost none are left. In the 1940s, the Jewish community of Tajikistan numbered nearly 30,000 people. Most were Persian-speaking Bukharan Jews who had lived in the region for millennia along with Ashkenazi Jews from Eastern Europe who resettled there in the Soviet era. The Jewish population is now estimated at less than 500, about half of whom live in Dushanbe.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Relationships between religious groups are generally amicable, although there is some concern among mainstream Muslim leaders<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (October 2010)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that minority religious groups undermine national unity. There is a concern for religious institutions becoming active in the political sphere. The <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Renaissance_Party_of_Tajikistan" title="Islamic Renaissance Party of Tajikistan">Islamic Renaissance Party</a> (IRP), a major combatant in the <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajikistan Civil War">1992–1997 Civil War</a> and then-proponent of the creation of an <a href="/wiki/State_religion#Islamic_states" title="State religion">Islamic state</a> in Tajikistan, constitutes no more than 30% of the government by statute.  Membership in <a href="/wiki/Hizb_ut-Tahrir" title="Hizb ut-Tahrir">Hizb ut-Tahrir</a>, a militant Islamic party which today aims for an overthrow of secular governments and the unification of Tajiks under one Islamic state, is illegal and members are subject to arrest and imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Numbers of large mosques appropriate for Friday prayers are limited and some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2012)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> feel this is discriminatory.
</p><p>By law, religious communities must register by the State Committee on Religious Affairs (SCRA) and with local authorities. Registration with the SCRA requires a charter, a list of 10 or more members, and evidence of local government approval prayer site location. Religious groups who do not have a physical structure are not allowed to gather publicly for prayer. Failure to register can result in large fines and closure of place of worship. There are reports that registration on the local level is sometimes difficult to obtain.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> People under the age of 18 are also barred from public religious practice.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of January 2016, as part of an "anti-radicalisation campaign", police in the Khatlon region reportedly shaved the beards of 13,000 men and shut down 160 shops selling the hijab. Shaving beards and discouraging women from wearing hijab is part of a government campaign targeting trends that are deemed "alien and inconsistent with Tajik culture", and "to preserve secular traditions".<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Tajikistan" title="Health in Tajikistan">Health in Tajikistan</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Hospital.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Big_Hospital.jpg/220px-Big_Hospital.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Big_Hospital.jpg/330px-Big_Hospital.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Big_Hospital.jpg/440px-Big_Hospital.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Hospital.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hospital in Dushanbe</div></div></div>
<p>Despite repeated efforts by the Tajik government to improve and expand health care, the system remains among the most underdeveloped and poor, with severe shortages of medical supplies. The state's Ministry of Labor and Social Welfare reported that 104,272 disabled people are registered in Tajikistan (2000). This group of people suffers most from poverty in Tajikistan. The government of Tajikistan and the World Bank considered activities to support this part of the population described in the World Bank's Poverty Reduction Strategy Paper.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Public expenditure on health was at 1% of the GDP in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth was estimated to be 66.38 years in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Infant_mortality" title="Infant mortality">infant mortality</a> rate was approximately 37 deaths per 1,000 children in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, there were 170 physicians per 100,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010 the country experienced an outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Polio" title="Polio">polio</a> that caused more than 457 cases of polio in both children and adults, and resulted in 29 deaths before being brought under control.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajik_National_University_(Main_Building).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tajik_National_University_%28Main_Building%29.jpg/220px-Tajik_National_University_%28Main_Building%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tajik_National_University_%28Main_Building%29.jpg/330px-Tajik_National_University_%28Main_Building%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Tajik_National_University_%28Main_Building%29.jpg/440px-Tajik_National_University_%28Main_Building%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1443" data-file-height="1077" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tajik_National_University_(Main_Building).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tajik_National_University" title="Tajik National University">Tajik National University</a> in Dushanbe</div></div></div>
<p>Despite its poverty, Tajikistan has a high rate of literacy due to the old Soviet system of free education, with an estimated 99.8% of the population having the ability to read and write.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_83-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Public education in Tajikistan consists of 11 years of primary and secondary education but the government has plans to implement a 12-year system in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-classbase.com_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-classbase.com-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> There is a relatively large number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Tajikistan" title="List of universities in Tajikistan">tertiary education institutions</a> including <a href="/wiki/Khujand_State_University" title="Khujand State University">Khujand State University</a> which has 76 departments in 15 faculties,<sup id="cite_ref-classbase.com_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-classbase.com-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan_State_University_of_Law,_Business,_%26_Politics" title="Tajikistan State University of Law, Business, &amp; Politics">Tajikistan State University of Law, Business, &amp; Politics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khorugh_State_University" title="Khorugh State University">Khorugh State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_University_of_Tajikistan" title="Agricultural University of Tajikistan">Agricultural University of Tajikistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tajik_National_University" title="Tajik National University">Tajik National University</a>, and several other institutions. Most, but not all, universities were established during the Soviet Era. As of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> tertiary education enrollment was 17%, significantly below the sub-regional average of 37%.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Many Tajiks left the education system due to low demand in the labour market for people with extensive educational training or professional skills.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Public spending on education was relatively constant between 2005–2012 and fluctuated from 3.5% to 4.1% of <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> significantly below the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> average of 6%.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_122-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> reported that the level of spending was "severely inadequate to meet the requirements of the country’s high-needs education system."<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_122-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a UNICEF-supported survey, about 25 percent of girls in Tajikistan fail to complete compulsory primary education because of poverty and gender bias,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> although <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> is generally high in Tajikistan.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Estimates of out of school children range from 4.6% to 19.4% with the vast majority being girls.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_122-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2017, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Central_Asia" title="University of Central Asia">University of Central Asia</a> will launch its second campus in Khorog, Tajikistan, offering majors in Earth &amp; Environmental Sciences and Economics.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tajikistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The national sport of Tajikistan is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gushtigiri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gushtigiri (page does not exist)">gushtigiri</a>, a form of traditional wrestling.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another popular sport is <a href="/wiki/Buzkashi" title="Buzkashi">buzkashi</a>, a game played on horseback, like <a href="/wiki/Polo" title="Polo">polo</a>. One plays it on one's own and in teams. The aim of the game is to grab a 50&#160;kg dead goat, ride clear of the other players, get back to the starting point and drop it in a designated circle. It is also practised in Afghanistan, Kyrgyzstan, Kazakhstan, Uzbekistan and Turkmenistan. It is often played at <a href="/wiki/Nowruz" title="Nowruz">Nowruz</a> celebrations.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_(20).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_%2820%29.jpg/220px-1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_%2820%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_%2820%29.jpg/330px-1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_%2820%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_%2820%29.jpg/440px-1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_%2820%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3405" data-file-height="2254" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1982_expedition_to_Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350_(20).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tajikistan is a popular destination amongst mountaineers. 1982 expedition to <a href="/wiki/Tartu_%C3%9Clikool_350" title="Tartu Ülikool 350">Tartu Ülikool 350</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Tajikistan's mountains provide many opportunities for outdoor sports, such as hill climbing, mountain biking, rock climbing, skiing, snowboarding, hiking, and mountain climbing. The facilities are limited, however. Mountain climbing and hiking tours to the Fann and Pamir Mountains, including the 7,000&#160;m peaks in the region, are seasonally organised by local and international alpine agencies.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is a popular sport in Tajikistan. The <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan_national_football_team" title="Tajikistan national football team">Tajikistan national football team</a> competes in <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">AFC</a> competitions. The top clubs in Tajikistan compete in the <a href="/wiki/Tajik_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Tajik League">Tajik League</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Tajikistan_Cricket_Federation" title="Tajikistan Cricket Federation">Tajikistan Cricket Federation</a> was formed in 2012 as the governing body for the sport of <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> in Tajikistan. It was granted affiliate membership of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Cricket_Council" title="Asian Cricket Council">Asian Cricket Council</a> in the same year.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Tajikistan" title="Rugby union in Tajikistan">Rugby union in Tajikistan</a> is a minor but growing sport.
</p><p>Four Tajikistani athletes have won Olympic medals for their country since independence. They are: wrestler <a href="/wiki/Yusup_Abdusalomov" title="Yusup Abdusalomov">Yusup Abdusalomov</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wrestling_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_freestyle_84_kg" title="Wrestling at the 2008 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s freestyle 84 kg">silver</a> in Beijing 2008), judoka <a href="/wiki/Rasul_Boqiev" title="Rasul Boqiev">Rasul Boqiev</a> (<a href="/wiki/Judo_at_the_2008_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_73_kg" title="Judo at the 2008 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s 73 kg">bronze</a> in Beijing 2008), boxer <a href="/wiki/Mavzuna_Chorieva" title="Mavzuna Chorieva">Mavzuna Chorieva</a> (<a href="/wiki/Boxing_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_lightweight" title="Boxing at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Women&#39;s lightweight">bronze</a> in London 2012) and hammer thrower <a href="/wiki/Dilshod_Nazarov" title="Dilshod Nazarov">Dilshod Nazarov</a> (<a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_hammer_throw" title="Athletics at the 2016 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s hammer throw">gold</a> in Rio de Janeiro 2016).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Khorugh" title="Khorugh">Khorugh</a>, capital of <a href="/wiki/Gorno-Badakhshan_Autonomous_Region" title="Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Region">Gorno-Badakhshan Autonomous Region</a>, is the location of highest altitude where <a href="/wiki/Bandy" title="Bandy">bandy</a> has been played.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tajikistan has also one <a href="/wiki/Ski_resort" title="Ski resort">ski resort</a>, called <a href="/wiki/Safed_Dara" title="Safed Dara">Safed Dara</a> (formerly <i>Takob</i>), near the town of <a href="/wiki/Varzob" title="Varzob">Varzob</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
